Introduction. After having read you your Father, this last science of medicine with its supplementary texts and the author's own statements and declarations, it has been my endeavor to complete this treatise on surgery using his instructions for operation by hand. (Note: This translation is an attempt at capturing the essence of a medieval Latin medical text discussing Albucasis’ work in chirurgery without additional commentary.)
Since surgery by hand is practiced within our region and at this time of the year entirely in our own hands; until perhaps it might perish as a science or be cut off from its source: that very thing has happened, namely because some have left their guide — those ancient books which were carried away with them. And for such error there came hesitation on part of others who had not followed this pathway into the secrets of surgery; until at last they find out what was intended by him himself and his eluc0id: It is my task to bring about completion through adherence to these instructions in this treatise, following both their directions as well as abbreviations. And so I shall accompany with tools for cauterization along with the rest of surgical instruments according to what has been stated by him and his preparation: when done properly it will fulfill my duty hereafter. (Note: This translation aims solely at rendering a medieval Latin medical text concerning Albucasis' work on surgery without additional commentary.)
Because the surgeon does not find it within this time due to: for medicine is a long-established art and requires its author's exercise beforehand in anatomy as described by Galen; until he knows the forms of body members, their connections with each other, bone structure (of ossicles), nerves including pulse rate and resting state—and that too concerning sea urchins along with gill count. As I witnessed a surgeon follow the apostema scrophulae on a woman'thy neck and pierce some of her arteries therein; that blood flowed from her until she bled to death in his hands.
And I saw another physician who requested to extract the large bone that had been processed at age... I then went to him, and extracted it with a chisel-like tool. Why was the man dead on the third day?
And I have already called for help; and indeed, I saw the size of the stone, and the positioning of the wound which would cause death.
And I saw another physician who accepted the staff of some lord's land in connection with medicine: and it happened that there was an eunuch dark-skinned at the time; he had a fracture near his heel, which the doctor treated ignorantly, tightening the wound above the ulna joint together with swolthy bands without attempting to release pressure from beneath.
Then released him according to his own prejudices. After that he sent him away for a few days and warned him not to strain the ligament again; thus it remained afflicted until corrupting sand was lodged in its foot, and his own leg ultimately led him astray into ruination.
I called to him and cured the strain of his ligament; consequently he found relief from pain and discomfort.

In the manner of treating leprosy with heat (cauterization). Here Albucasis is directing how one should apply his methods specifically for
For lepers when they are taken to the operation of cutting (cauterization), it is done at its greatest extent. And especially the leprosy (which is caused by decay of humours and melancholy): so when considering cutting for this disease, take that into account as well.
Therefore if leprosy is incipient and you have treated it with the cutting method we've discussed beforehand (cauterization), ensuring that it does not descend or weaken: once a patient who becomes ill again, encompassing corruption of his entire body constitution; then cut on its head five times as follows: one in the middle of the head to mark and cauterize, another at the forehead's end (near the hairline), two above each earlobe, and one behind the nape.
And lastly with the remaining part of your instrument when performing cutting (cauterization), make an impression in the mouth and remove fragments from there: to soothe expulsion of thick phlegm produced by it; also cauterize over what has been cut, according as necessity demands.
But if leprosy is now sparse upon the ill and appears manifestly; then it becomes necessary to perform cutting using these instruments we mentioned for the head (the five cauterizations on top of), as well as over its nose, two cutters at each upper jaw, twice up both spinal pillars, six times across backbones themselves, a large one above tail vertebrae and another just within itself in alignment with: also pairs for the ancles (atop): once upon all ancle entirely, paired on either side of joints between legs; two at each humerus bone; twos up both wrists. Furthermore apply cutting to every intersection where fingers meet hands and feet respectively—and above heel stone with tool handles: cauterize these areas as needed for the disease's treatment alongside previously employed methods of cautery on topical lesions, joint extremities, backbones, arms, wrist area, feet including sole (heel stones), fingers/toes and where hands meet them.
And cut off those nerves at the very end of the heel so that they do not burn.
And when it cauterizes above the lips and also over the stomach and elsewhere on the epigastric region (the upper central part of the abdomen just below the chest).
